# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox CSS calc() Value Overflow

## Your Task

Firefox crashes when processing CSS calc() with extreme values. Find the C++ source files in mozilla/gecko-dev that (1) parse CSS calc() expressions and (2) handle numeric overflow during calc() value resolution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about Firefox's CSS calc() overflow issue:

### Key Files Identified:

1. **servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs** - Core calc() expression resolution with the `resolve_internal()` function that performs arithmetic operations

2. **servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs** - Computed value resolution for calc() length-percentage values

3. **servo/ports/geckolib/glue.rs** - C++ binding layer containing `Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage()` that calls the Rust resolver

4. **layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h** - C++ header with `StyleCalcLengthPercentage::ResolveToCSSPixels()` that triggers resolution

### Critical Overflow Points:

- **Line 941 (generics/calc.rs)**: Invert operation performs `1.0 / v` which can overflow with extreme values
- **Lines 66-86 (generics/calc.rs)**: ModRemOp::apply() performs division operations that can overflow
- **Lines 1133-1149 (generics/calc.rs)**: ModRem resolution calls the division operations

The root cause is that Firefox's Stylo (Rust-based styling engine) performs arithmetic operations on floating-point values during calc() resolution without proper overflow guards, allowing NaN and infinity values to propagate and potentially crash the browser.

    "content": "1: /* This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\n2:  * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this\n3:  * file, You can obtain one at https://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */\n4: \n5: //! `<length-percentage>` computed values, and related ones.\n6: //!\n7: //! The over-all design is a tagged pointer, with the lower bits of the pointer\n8: //! being non-zero if it is a non-calc value.\n9: //!\n10: //! It is expected to take 64 bits both in x86 and x86-64. This is implemented\n11: //! as a `union`, with 4 different variants:\n12: //!\n13: //!  * The length and percentage variants have a { tag, f32 } (effectively)\n14: //!    layout. The tag has to overlap with the lower 2 bits of the calc variant.\n15: //!\n16: //!  * The `calc()` variant is a { tag, pointer } in x86 (so same as the\n17: //!    others), or just a { pointer } in x86-64 (so that the two bits of the tag\n18: //!    can be obtained from the lower bits of the pointer).\n19: //!\n20: //!  * There's a `tag` variant just to make clear when only the tag is intended\n21: //!    to be read. Note that the tag needs to be masked always by `TAG_MASK`, to\n22: //!    deal with the pointer variant in x86-64.\n23: //!\n24: //! The assertions in the constructor methods ensure that the tag getter matches\n25: //! our expectations.\n26: \n27: use super::{position::AnchorSide, Context, Length, Percentage, ToComputedValue};\n28:
